Persons in possession, or the person under whom the occupant holds the land, may compel the parties to any such champertous contract to testify on the trial, or to make discovery by answer to petition in equity. The person so compelled to give evidence or to make discovery shall not be subjected thereby to any penal or criminal prosecution for champerty and maintenance, and the evidence or discovery shall not be used in any such prosecution.

History

History.
213.

Annotations

 NOTES TO DECISIONS 

  Cited: 

 Commonwealth v. Brown, 619 S.W.2d 699, 1981 Ky. LEXIS 263 (Ky. 1981), overruled, Murphy v. Commonwealth, 652 S.W.2d 69, 1983 Ky. LEXIS 249 (Ky. 1983), overruled in part, Murphy v. Commonwealth, 652 S.W.2d 69, 1983 Ky. LEXIS 249 (Ky. 1983).


372.110.  Person in possession may purchase adverse claim.

Text

Persons in possession may purchase the adverse outstanding title or claim. The purchase shall be good and shall inure to the benefit of the person making it, or to the person under whom he claims and holds the land so possessed.

History

History.
214.

Annotations

 NOTES TO DECISIONS 

1. Deed to Adverse Possessor.

2. Purchase by Adverse Possessor.

3. Coowners.

4.  Tortious Acquisition.

5.  Ouster of Adverse Possessor by Third Party.

  1. Deed to Adverse Possessor. 

 A deed to the adverse possessor was valid. (decided under prior law) Adams v. Buford, 36 Ky. 406, 1838 Ky. LEXIS 76 (Ky. 1838). See Chiles v. Jones, 37 Ky. 528, 1838 Ky. LEXIS 177 (Ky. 1838).

 A deed to one in adverse possession is not “champertous.” Williams v. Thomas, 285 Ky. 776, 149 S.W.2d 525, 1941 Ky. LEXIS 470 (Ky. 1941).

  2. Purchase by Adverse Possessor. 

 The adverse possessor may purchase an outstanding claim without interrupting his adverse possession against another. Bryant v. Prewitt, 132 Ky. 799, 117 S.W. 343, 1909 Ky. LEXIS 153 (Ky. 1909).

  3. Coowners. 

 One who held half a tract for himself and half as trustee and who purchased an outstanding adverse claim acted jointly for himself and the beneficiary, and the latter had to pay for his proportionate part. (decided under prior law) M'Clanahan's Heirs v. Henderson's Heirs, 9 Ky. 388, 1820 Ky. LEXIS 97 (Ky. 1820).

 Purchase of an outstanding adverse claim by one joint owner inured to the joint benefit of all the owners unless the cotenancy was definitely renounced. (decided under prior law) Thruston v. Masterson, 39 Ky. 228, 1839 Ky. LEXIS 124 (Ky. 1839); Vallandingham v. Johnson, 85 Ky. 288, 3 S.W. 173, 8 Ky. L. Rptr. 940, 1887 Ky. LEXIS 45 (Ky. 1887).

 Purchase of an outstanding adverse claim by one joint owner inures to the joint benefit of all the owners, unless the cotenancy is definitely renounced. Webb v. Webb, 200 Ky. 488, 255 S.W. 137, 1923 Ky. LEXIS 142 (Ky. 1923).

  4.  Tortious Acquisition. 

 It was immaterial that possession was acquired tortiously. (decided under prior law) Adams v. Buford, 36 Ky. 406, 1838 Ky. LEXIS 76 (Ky. 1838).

  5.  Ouster of Adverse Possessor by Third Party. 

 An agreement between the title holder and another whereby the latter was to forcibly oust an adverse possessor and then receive a deed to the title was champertous. (decided under prior law) Adams v. Buford, 36 Ky. 406, 1838 Ky. LEXIS 76 (Ky. 1838).

 Research References and Practice Aids 

  Northern Kentucky Law Review. 

Kentucky Law Survey, Youngs, A Compendium of Cases on Future Interests in Kentucky, 6 N. Ky. L. Rev. 283 (1979).

  Treatises 

Caldwell’s Kentucky Form Book, 5th Ed., Practice Context for Adverse Possession, § 303.00.


372.120.  No right of action on champertous contract.

Text

Neither party to any contract made in violation of any of the provisions of KRS 372.060 to 372.120 shall have any right of action thereon.

History

History.
216.

Annotations

 NOTES TO DECISIONS 

1. Applicability.

2. Assignment.

3. Champerty as Defense Only.

4.  Forfeiture.

  1. Applicability. 

 The forfeiture applies to the champertous contract, not to the contract on which it may have been based. Wemhoff v. Rutherford, 98 Ky. 91, 32 S.W. 288, 17 Ky. L. Rptr. 659, 1895 Ky. LEXIS 21 (Ky. 1895); Cumberland Tel. & Tel. Co. v. Maxberry, 134 Ky. 642, 121 S.W. 447, 1909 Ky. LEXIS 410 (Ky. 1909); Keeney v. Waters, 135 Ky. 525, 122 S.W. 837, 1909 Ky. LEXIS 316 (Ky. 1909).

 This section does not bar a right to rescind a sale made contrary to KRS 372.070. It applies only to contracts and conveyances made in violation of KRS 372.060. Meade v. Ratliff, 133 Ky. 411, 118 S.W. 271, 1909 Ky. LEXIS 183 (Ky. 1909).

  2. Assignment. 

 Neither a champertous assignment of a note nor a judgment upon it conveys title. Roberts v. Yancey, 14 Ky. L. Rptr. 42, aff'd, Godfrey v. Commonwealth, 21 S.W. 1047, 15 Ky. L. Rptr. 3 (1893), aff'd, 94 Ky. 243, 21 S.W. 1047, 15 Ky. L. Rptr. 10, 1893 Ky. LEXIS 32 (Ky. 1893).

  3. Champerty as Defense Only. 

 Champerty under KRS 372.060 can only be pleaded by a party thereto as a defense, except when a creditor transfers a cause of action to a third person who is to receive a part of the proceeds for prosecuting the case. Wemhoff v. Rutherford, 98 Ky. 91, 32 S.W. 288, 17 Ky. L. Rptr. 659, 1895 Ky. LEXIS 21 (Ky. 1895). See Aetna Life Ins. Co. v. Weck, 163 Ky. 37, 173 S.W. 317, 1915 Ky. LEXIS 181 (Ky. 1915).

  4.  Forfeiture. 

 The forfeiture applied to the champertous contract, not to the contract on which it might have been based. (decided under prior law) Boone v. Chiles, 35 U.S. 177, 9 L. Ed. 388, 1836 U.S. LEXIS 429 (U.S. 1836).


372.130.  Forfeitures not to apply to certain cases.

Text

None of the forfeitures declared by KRS 372.060 to 372.120 apply to cases of controversy between lessor and lessee, mortgagor and mortgagee, vendor and vendee or trustee and beneficiary.

History

History.
215.

Annotations

 NOTES TO DECISIONS 

  1. Exemptions from Forfeiture. 

 In an action by a vendor of land to recover damages for deceit practiced by the vendee, the vendor is exempted from forfeitures for executing a contract champertous under KRS 372.060. Akers v. Martin, 110 Ky. 335, 61 S.W. 465, 1901 Ky. LEXIS 90 (Ky. 1901).


372.140.  Power of attorney to confess judgment — Release of errors.

Text

(1) Except as provided in KRS 457.150, any power of attorney to confess judgment or to suffer judgment to pass by default or otherwise, and any release of errors, given before an action is instituted, is void.

(2) No person shall appear for a defendant under any such power in any court in this state.

History

HISTORY:
416, 417; 2018 ch. 185, § 28, effective July 14, 2018.

Annotations

 NOTES TO DECISIONS 

1. Agreements in Violation.

2. Agreements Not in Violation.

3. Conflict of Laws.

4. Contracts Containing Powers to Confess.

5. Entry of Appearance.

6. Consent Judgments.

  1. Agreements in Violation. 

 The prohibition applied to both powers and releases executed before filing of suit. (decided under prior law) Ward & Johnson v. Curcier, 11 Ky. 202, 1822 Ky. LEXIS 73 (Ky. 1822).

 Powers of attorney to confess judgment executed before filing of suit were void. (decided under prior law) O'Hara v. Lannier, 40 Ky. 100, 1840 Ky. LEXIS 92 (Ky. 1840).

 Judgment entered by joint motion of counsel on an award recorded several years after the dismissal of the original suit was void, since the joinder by defendant’s counsel in the motion for judgment without any suit pending was in effect a confession of judgment prior to suit. (decided under prior law) Hay v. Cole, 50 Ky. 70, 1850 Ky. LEXIS 20 (Ky. 1850).

 Powers of attorney to confess judgment and releases of error executed by a defendant to plaintiff’s attorney were against public policy under any circumstances. (decided under prior law) Ball v. Poor, 81 Ky. 26, 4 Ky. L. Rptr. 746, 1883 Ky. LEXIS 23 (Ky. Ct. App. 1883).

 A power of attorney executed by a defendant authorizing plaintiff’s attorney to enter his appearance in an action not yet filed violated law that provided that power of attorney to confess judgment and releases of error given before action was instituted were void. (decided under prior law) Ball v. Poor, 81 Ky. 26, 4 Ky. L. Rptr. 746, 1883 Ky. LEXIS 23 (Ky. Ct. App. 1883).

 An answer executed prior to suit at the instance of a plaintiff or his attorney entering a defendant’s appearance, admitting the allegation of the petition, or confessing judgment, violates this section, and a judgment rendered thereon without process or other appearance is void. Hudson v. McMahon, 50 S.W. 259 (Ky. 1899); Aultman & Taylor Co. v. Mead, 109 Ky. 583, 60 S.W. 294, 22 Ky. L. Rptr. 1189, 1901 Ky. LEXIS 17 (Ky. 1901); Aultman & Taylor Co. v. Meade, 121 Ky. 241, 89 S.W. 137, 28 Ky. L. Rptr. 208, 1905 Ky. LEXIS 193 (Ky. 1905).

  2. Agreements Not in Violation. 

 Powers of attorney to confess judgment executed after instituting suit were not prohibited. (decided under prior law) Ward & Johnson v. Curcier, 11 Ky. 202, 1822 Ky. LEXIS 73 (Ky. 1822); Ball v. Poor, 81 Ky. 26, 4 Ky. L. Rptr. 746, 1883 Ky. LEXIS 23 (Ky. Ct. App. 1883).

 In a suit for the sale of land, payment of liens and division of proceeds, the fact that the guardian of an infant plaintiff was also attorney for a defendant lienholder was not violative of this section. Baxter Realty Co. v. Martin, 185 Ky. 697, 216 S.W. 110, 1919 Ky. LEXIS 361 (Ky. 1919).

 Judgment entered on stipulation of settlement agreement was not barred by this section, since it was neither a judgment by confession nor a judgment entered before an action was instituted. All States Investors, Inc. v. Bankers Bond Co., 343 F.2d 618, 1965 U.S. App. LEXIS 5972 (6th Cir. Ky.), cert. denied, 382 U.S. 830, 86 S. Ct. 69, 15 L. Ed. 2d 74, 1965 U.S. LEXIS 679 (U.S. 1965).

  3. Conflict of Laws. 

 Judgment obtained in Illinois under power of attorney to confess judgment on note, signed in Kentucky but delivered and payable in Illinois, was entitled to full faith and credit and would be enforced by Kentucky courts. Wedding v. First Nat'l Bank, Inc., 280 Ky. 610, 133 S.W.2d 931, 1939 Ky. LEXIS 175 (Ky. 1939).

  4. Contracts Containing Powers to Confess. 

 An obligation containing authority to confess judgment is not wholly void, since the illegal portion is separable. Farmers' Bank of White Plains v. Bass, 218 Ky. 813, 292 S.W. 489, 1927 Ky. LEXIS 258 (Ky. 1927).

  5. Entry of Appearance. 

 Entry of appearance may be made by an attorney of defendant acting under specific employment in that case but cannot be entered by an attorney acting under general retainer, and cannot be entered by an attorney under any circumstances if his interests conflict with those of his client or if he is personally interested in the subject matter. King Const. Co. v. Mary Helen Coal Corp., 194 Ky. 435, 239 S.W. 799, 1922 Ky. LEXIS 184 (Ky. 1922).

  6. Consent Judgments. 

 This section is intended to prevent cognovit clauses in contracts giving creditors the authority, at some later date, to confess a judgment against a debtor without giving him or her the opportunity to defend; it cannot be said to apply to agreed judgments voluntarily and knowingly entered into between parties. Ashland Armco Employees Credit Union v. Cantrell, 685 S.W.2d 559, 1984 Ky. App. LEXIS 582 (Ky. Ct. App. 1984).

 An agreed judgment entered into between a credit union and a debtor by which the credit union in part consented to relinquish its right to demand immediate payment of the full balance due, in exchange for a promise to make monthly payments, was in essence a consent judgment, a private contract entered into between parties and sanctioned by order of court; it did not and could not confer a power of attorney to subsequently confess judgment against the debtor. Ashland Armco Employees Credit Union v. Cantrell, 685 S.W.2d 559, 1984 Ky. App. LEXIS 582 (Ky. Ct. App. 1984).

 Research References and Practice Aids 

  Cross-References. 

Confession of judgment after action is instituted, KRS 454.090.

  Kentucky Law Journal. 

Blake, Conflict of Laws — Apparent Trends in Jurisdiction, 34 Ky. L.J. 139 (1946).


372.160.  Mailing that contains item that appears to be check — Disclosure of consequences of signing — Offer for contract formation not valid without disclosure — Notice relating to time limit — Delivery of goods or services does not form contract — Remedies — Jurisdiction.

Text

(1) Any term which is defined in the Uniform Commercial Code, KRS Chapter 355, shall have that same meaning in this section, unless the context otherwise requires.

(2) Any person soliciting business in this Commonwealth who intends to make an offer for contract formation by sending through the mail, as part of the solicitation, what appears to be a check or other item payable to the recipient where the indorsement and subsequent negotiation of the item by the recipient is intended by any party to the item, or agent or assignee thereof, to form an acceptance of the contract shall make the following disclosure in upper case twelve (12) point bold face type immediately adjacent to the designated place of indorsement: “BY SIGNING AND DELIVERING THIS DOCUMENT YOU AGREE TO PAY FOR FUTURE SERVICES ARISING OUT OF THIS CONTRACT.”.

(3) A purported offer described in subsection (2) of this section that does not contain the required disclosure, to the extent a subsequent indorsement and negotiation of the item would otherwise constitute an acceptance, shall not be a valid offer for contract formation in this Commonwealth.

(4) If a purported offer which meets the requirements in subsection (2) of this section relates to a free membership period, trial period, or some other similar acceptance incentive that is prescribed by a time limit and which purports to form a contract without a cancellation, rescission, revocation, or other form of termination by the recipient prior to the end of such a period, then the offeror shall send notice to the recipient at least two (2) weeks prior to the end of that time period of the recipient’s purported obligation to cancel, rescind, revoke, or otherwise terminate the recipient’s purported acceptance before a purported contract is formed. The notice shall be readily apparent on any communication from the offeror and it shall be in upper case twelve (12) point bold face type and in the following form: “YOU MUST ACT NOW TO AVOID FUTURE CHARGES.” Any time period described under this subsection that is part of a purported offer described in subsection (2) of this section and that is less than two (2) weeks shall not be a valid offer for contract formation in this Commonwealth.

(5) If a purported offer described in subsection (2) of this section does not contain the required disclosure, or is not followed by the required notice, then any goods or services delivered to the recipient pursuant to the purported offer shall not operate to form a contract by or between the offeror and the recipient. Any such offer or purported contract as a result thereof is void as against the public policy of the Commonwealth.

(6) An attempt by an offeror, or an agent or assignee thereof, to enforce a purported contract or to bind a recipient to a purported acceptance arising out of a purported offer that does not comply with this section shall be a violation of the Consumer Protection Act, KRS 367.170 to 367.300. Remedies available for a violation of KRS 367.170 to 367.300 shall be in addition to any remedies available at common law or under this section.

(7) The Attorney General, Commonwealth’s attorneys, and county attorneys shall have concurrent jurisdiction to enforce the provisions of this section in a court of the county where the purported offer was received.

(8) Any waiver by the recipient of jurisdiction for actions arising out of a purported offer under this section shall be void. Any depository bank or holder in due course of an item which does not meet the requirements of subsection (2) of this section or, as the case may be subsection (4) of this section, shall be held harmless by the offeror of the item, or an agent or assignee thereof.

(9) Nothing contained in this section shall apply to licensed lenders that are regulated by the Commonwealth of Kentucky, or to a bank regulated by the federal government or any agency thereof.

History

History.
Enact. Acts 2002, ch. 216, § 1, effective July 15, 2002.


372.990.  Penalties.

Text

Any person who violates any of the provisions of subsection (2) of KRS 372.140 shall forfeit one thousand dollars ($1,000) to the defendant, and shall be liable to damages at the suit of the party aggrieved.

History

History.
417, 418.

Annotations

 NOTES TO DECISIONS 

  1. Conflict of Laws. 

 The fact that KRS 372.140 forbids confession of judgment against makers and guarantor without process before maturity did not prevent Kentucky court giving full faith and credit to an Illinois judgment against a Kentucky surety where the parties intended the transaction should be governed by the Illinois law. Wedding v. First Nat'l Bank, Inc., 280 Ky. 610, 133 S.W.2d 931, 1939 Ky. LEXIS 175 (Ky. 1939).

  Cited: 

 Ashland Armco Employees Credit Union v. Cantrell, 685 S.W.2d 559, 1984 Ky. App. LEXIS 582 (Ky. Ct. App. 1984).
